import torch
import torch.nn as nn

# Default ModelNew is PyTorch-only. run_and_check: use check_kernel=False with backend=cuda
# until the candidate file contains a real CUDA kernel (see kernel_static_checker).

class Model(nn.Module):
    """
    Fused 1D convolution + GroupNorm for temporal sequences (N, C, T).

    Typical in time-series heads, audio / motor trajectories, and sequence models
    that use strided or padded Conv1d followed by per-channel normalization without
    collapsing the time dimension (GroupNorm over `out_channels` on (N, C_out, T')).

    Reference fusion target: `Conv1d` → `GroupNorm` (no activation), matching a
    common stem or residual branch in temporal backbones.
    """

    def __init__(
        self,
        in_channels: int,
        out_channels: int,
        num_groups: int,
        kernel_size: int = 3,
        stride: int = 1,
        padding: int = 1,
        dilation: int = 1,
        eps: float = 1e-5,
        affine: bool = True,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        assert out_channels % num_groups == 0
        self.conv = nn.Conv1d(
            in_channels,
            out_channels,
            kernel_size,
            stride=stride,
            padding=padding,
            dilation=dilation,
            bias=False,
        )
        self.norm = nn.GroupNorm(
            num_groups=num_groups,
            num_channels=out_channels,
            eps=eps,
            affine=affine,
        )

    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        """
        Args:
            x: (N, C_in, T) temporal feature map
        Returns:
            (N, C_out, T') with T' determined by conv stride / padding / kernel
        """
        return self.norm(self.conv(x))


class ModelNew(nn.Module):
    """
    KernelBench candidate entry point. Replace with a fused CUDA/Triton kernel;
    default delegates to `Model` for harness smoke tests.
    """

    def __init__(
        self,
        in_channels: int,
        out_channels: int,
        num_groups: int,
        kernel_size: int = 3,
        stride: int = 1,
        padding: int = 1,
        dilation: int = 1,
        eps: float = 1e-5,
        affine: bool = True,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        self._impl = Model(
            in_channels,
            out_channels,
            num_groups,
            kernel_size=kernel_size,
            stride=stride,
            padding=padding,
            dilation=dilation,
            eps=eps,
            affine=affine,
        )

    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        return self._impl(x)


batch_size = 16
in_channels = 128
out_channels = 256
num_groups = 32
seq_len = 1024
kernel_size = 3
stride = 1
padding = 1


def get_inputs():
    x = torch.randn(batch_size, in_channels, seq_len)
    return [x]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [
        in_channels,
        out_channels,
        num_groups,
        kernel_size,
        stride,
        padding,
    ]

reasoning
We need to write a custom CUDA kernel that fuses Conv1d and GroupNorm for temporal sequences (N, C, T). The kernel should be faster than the reference (which uses PyTorch's cuDNN conv + cuDNN/optimized GroupNorm). We need to produce numerically equivalent outputs (fp32, atol=rtol=1e-4). Given the constraints, we need to think about how to fuse these operations efficiently on GPU. First, let's understand the problem dimensions: - Input: (N, C_in, T) - Conv1d: C_in -> C_out, kernel_size, stride, padding, dilation, bias=False - GroupNorm: num_groups groups over C_out channels, eps, affine (scale and bias) Typical sizes: batch_size=16, in_channels=128, out_channels=256, num_groups=32, seq_len=1024, kernel_size=3, stride=1, padding=1. So after conv, output is (N, C_out, T_out) where T_out = floor((T + 2*padding - dilation*(kernel_size-1) - 1)/stride + 1). With stride=1, padding=1, dilation=1, kernel_size=3: T_out = T = 1024. The naive approach: compute conv first, then group norm. Fusing them avoids writing the intermediate conv output to global memory and reading it back for group norm. Since bias=False in conv, the conv output y[n,c,t] = sum_k sum_{i=0}^{K-1} weight[c, k, i] * x[n, k, t'], where t' is the input index depending on padding, stride, dilation. GroupNorm: for each sample n and group g, compute mean and variance over channels in group and time dimension. Specifically: - groups = num_groups - channels per group = C_out / num_groups - For each n, g: mean = (1/(C_g * T_out)) sum_{c in group g} sum_{t=0}^{T_out-1} y[n,c,t] - var = (1/(C_g * T_out)) sum_{c in group g} sum_t (y[n,c,t] - mean)^2 - Then normalize: y_hat[n,c,t] = (y[n,c,t] - mean) / sqrt(var + eps) - If affine: y_out[n,c,t] = gamma[c] * y_hat[n,c,t] + beta[c] We can fuse this by having each block compute a chunk of the output, possibly accumulating conv results and then doing group norm on the fly. However, fusing conv + group norm is complex because group norm requires reductions over channels and time. A strategy: 1. Compute conv output tile per block. 2. Within a block, we might have to compute partial sums for mean/var and then do a second pass or use shared memory to store the full group's output. Given that C_out=256, groups=32, so channels per group = 8. T_out=1024. So each group has 8*1024 = 8192 elements. That's not too large. N=16. Total elements = 16*256*1024 = 4,194,304. One approach: - Launch a kernel where each block processes one (n, g) group. It loads the input x required for the group's channels, computes the conv output for all channels in the group and all time steps, writes to shared memory or registers, then computes mean and variance, then applies normalization and affine, and writes to global memory. But each group has 8 channels and 1024 time steps. The conv for each output element uses C_in * kernel_size weights. For each group (8 output channels), we need to compute 8*1024 output elements. Each output element requires dot product of length C_in*K = 128*3 = 384. So total MACs per group = 8*1024*384 = 3,145,728. With N=16, total MACs = ~50M. To compute conv for a whole group, we could have each thread compute one or more output elements. 8*1024 = 8192 elements per group. If we use 256 threads per block, each thread computes 32 output elements. Or we can tile by time and channel. But the main challenge is accessing x. For conv1d with kernel_size=3, stride=1, padding=1, each output time t requires input times t-1, t, t+1 (with padding). So we can load x into shared memory, but x has C_in=128 channels. For a tile of time, say 128 time steps, we'd need 128*130 elements of x (with halo). At fp32, that's 128*130*4 = 66KB, which might exceed shared memory per block (48KB or 100KB depending on GPU). But we can tile by channels or time. Alternatively, we can compute the conv in a straightforward way: each thread computes one output element y[n,c,t] by iterating over in_channels and kernel_size, loading weights from constant memory or global memory. Since weight is small (256*128*3 = 98304 floats = ~384KB), it might fit in L2 cache. Or we can load weights into shared memory per block. Since the kernel is small (3), and in_channels=128, we can have each thread compute a single output element directly. Then we need to aggregate across threads for group norm. But each thread only holds one value; we need to compute mean and variance across all elements in the group. So a block of threads could process one (n,g). For example, a block with 1024 threads could process all time steps for one channel. But we have 8 channels per group. Alternatively, a block of 512 threads could process 512 time points across all 8 channels? That's 64 time points per channel. A better approach: have each block compute all elements for one (n, g) group. Use shared memory to store the group's output temporarily. With 8 channels * 1024 time = 8192 floats = 32KB. That easily fits in shared memory! So we can compute the conv output for all elements in the group, store them in shared memory, then compute mean and variance using shared memory reductions, then normalize and write to global memory. This seems very feasible. Let's design the kernel: Grid dimensions: (N, num_groups) blocks. Each block handles one sample and one group. Block dimensions: let's say 256 threads. Each thread computes multiple output elements. Total elements per group = C_g * T_out = (C_out/num_groups) * T_out. Let C_g = channels_per_group = C_out / num_groups. Let T = T_out. For the example: C_g=8, T=1024. Total elements = 8192. With 256 threads, each thread handles 32 elements. We can distribute them in a 1D layout: thread i computes elements with linear index idx = i + j*blockDim.x for j=0,...,num_iters-1. Mapping linear index to (c_in_group, t): c_in_group = idx / T, t = idx % T. But to ensure coalesced access, we might want threads in a warp to access contiguous memory. If we store shared memory as [C_g][T] row-major (C_g is the channel within group, T is time), then contiguous threads accessing contiguous t for same c is coalesced. But each thread computing a strided set might not be optimal. Alternatively, each thread can handle a contiguous chunk of t for a specific c. Simplify: we can have each block process one (n,g), with blockDim.x = 256. We can compute the number of iterations needed to cover all C_g * T elements. For i in range(blockDim.x): for linear_idx = i + j*blockDim.x (j=0..ceil(total/blockDim.x)-1): if linear_idx < total: c = linear_idx / T t = linear_idx % T compute conv for output channel = g*C_g + c, time t. To compute conv: out = 0 c_out = g*C_g + c for k in range(in_channels): for K_idx in range(kernel_size): t_in = t * stride - padding + K_idx * dilation if t_in >= 0 and t_in < seq_len: out += weight[c_out, k, K_idx] * x[n, k, t_in] We need to load weight and x. weight is (out_channels, in_channels, kernel_size). x is (N, in_channels, seq_len). We need to be careful about indexing. PyTorch Conv1d weight shape is (out_channels, in_channels//groups?, kernel_size). Wait, for standard nn.Conv1d, weight shape is (out_channels, in_channels // groups, kernel_size) only if groups > 1. Here groups is not a parameter of conv; it's for group norm. Similarly, for x, the block needs to access all in_channels * seq_len elements for sample n. That's 128*1024 = 131072 floats = 512KB. No, for fixed t, x[n, k, t] has stride T across k). So x[n, k, t] is not contiguous in k for fixed t? Let's check: memory layout: x[n, 0, 0], x[n, 0, 1], ..., x[n, 0, T-1], x[n, 1, 0], ... So for fixed t, x[n, k, t] is spaced by T. So not contiguous. But for fixed k, x[n, k, t] is contiguous. In our conv, for each output element (c_out, t), we iterate over k (in_channels) and K_idx (kernel_size). The access pattern for a given thread is: - x[n, k, t_in] where t_in changes with K_idx but k changes over the whole in_channels. For a fixed t_in, x[n, :, t_in] is strided by T. Reduction over 8192 elements with 256 threads: - We can do a tree reduction. Each thread can load a few elements from smem, accumulate sum and sum of squares, then reduce across warps using warp shuffles, then combine across warps using shared memory. For stride=1, padding=1, dilation=1, kernel_size=3, t_in ranges from t-1 to t+1. When threads in warp access x[n, k, t_in] where t_in differs by 1 across threads, that's contiguous in memory (since t is the fastest dimension). Good. For each iteration of k, the threads access x[n, k, t_in] for varying t_in. Since k changes in outer loop, these accesses are strided by seq_len. But across the warp, t_in values are contiguous, so the access pattern for a fixed k is contiguous in memory? x layout is N, C, T. For fixed n and k, x[n,k,:] is contiguous. So x[n,k,t_in] for contiguous t_in are contiguous. So within a warp, we access contiguous memory. This is perfectly coalesced. Great. But we have an inner loop over k from 0 to in_channels-1. But because all threads access the same k at the same time, they'll all load from x + n*C*T + k*T + t_in. The base address for each thread differs by t_in. Since t_in are contiguous, this is a contiguous segment of memory of length warpSize. So it's coalesced into one or two cache lines. Good. Thus, memory access pattern is efficient. However, we have to consider the efficiency of loading weight_smem. Each warp accesses weight for warp_id. Since different warps access different warp_id, there would be bank conflicts if they all read from shared memory simultaneously. But they are reading different channels, so the indices differ by in_channels*kernel_size. With 32 banks, if in_channels*kernel_size is a multiple of 32, there might be conflicts. in_channels=128, kernel_size=3, product=384, which is a multiple of 32? 384/32 = 12. So yes, each warp's weight starts at an offset multiple of 12*32 = 384 floats = 1536 bytes = 384*4 = 1536 bytes. Bank width is 4 bytes, so 1536 bytes corresponds to bank 0 again. All warps reading at offset 0 within their own block would map to the same bank? Wait, let's compute. Shared memory is arranged in 32 banks of 4 bytes each. Address a maps to bank (a/4) % 32. Warp 0 reads address 0 + idx. Warp 1 reads address 384 + idx. Bank for warp1 = (384 + idx)/4 % 32 = (96 + idx/4) % 32. Since 96 % 32 = 0, the bank is idx/4 % 32, same as warp0. So all warps will have bank conflicts if they read the same idx simultaneously. However, each warp is independent and can be scheduled at different times, but within a block they are executing concurrently. Bank conflicts occur when multiple threads in a warp access different addresses mapping to the same bank. But here, it's different warps. Bank conflicts are per warp. Each warp's threads are reading different offsets within the same channel's weights. For a given warp, threads read weight_smem[warp_offset + k*kernel_size + K]. If adjacent threads in the warp read the same time t but iterate over k and K in serial, then within the warp, all threads read the same weight values (since weight doesn't depend on t). Actually, for a given channel and given k,K, all threads in the warp need the same weight value (same c_out, same k, same K). So they all read the same shared memory address! That's a broadcast, not a bank conflict. Shared memory broadcasts are fast (one transaction). Good. What about x loads? All threads read different t_in, so contiguous addresses. Good. What about writing to smem? Each thread writes to smem[warp_id * T + t]. For a fixed warp, threads write to addresses separated by 1 float (contiguous). That's coalesced within warp and no bank conflicts (each thread hits a different bank). For different warps, they write to different regions, but again, per warp it's fine. This design seems very good. Now, we need to handle reduction for mean and var. After writing conv outputs to smem, we need __syncthreads(). Then we can compute the sum and sum of squares over smem. Total elements = C_g * T. For our example, 8192. We have 256 threads. So each thread can process 32 elements. But after we compute the sum, we need the mean, and then we need to compute sum of squared differences from mean. We can either: Approach 1: Two-pass algorithm. - First pass: compute sum (mean). - Second pass: compute sum of (x - mean)^2. This requires storing the data in smem and reading it twice. Since smem is fast, this is okay. Approach 2: Online variance (Welford). We can compute mean and M2 in one pass across the elements assigned to each thread, then reduce across the block. This is also efficient. But the data is in shared memory, so it's easy to do two passes. Let's do two passes for simplicity and numerical stability. However, we need to be careful: the data in smem is conv output. We can do: // Pass 1: compute local sum per thread float local_sum = 0.0f; for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < C_g * T; idx += blockDim.x) { local_sum += smem[idx]; } // warp reduce // block reduce __shared__ float block_sum; if (threadIdx.x == 0) block_sum = 0; __syncthreads(); // after warp reduce, atomicAdd or store to smem and reduce. Better: we can use a standard block reduction. Implementation of block reduce: - Each warp computes warp_sum using warp shuffles. - Store warp_sum in shared memory array warp_sums[32] (max warps per block). - Then first warp reads warp_sums and reduces to block_sum. Same for sum of squares. Then mean = block_sum / (C_g * T). Then each thread computes local_sq_diff: for idx = threadIdx.x; idx < C_g * T; idx += blockDim.x { float diff = smem[idx] - mean; local_sq_diff += diff * diff; } Then block reduce local_sq_diff -> block_sq_diff. Var = block_sq_diff / (C_g * T). (Note: GroupNorm uses biased or unbiased variance? PyTorch GroupNorm computes variance as 1/(C_g * T) sum((x-mean)^2). Let's verify.) Looking at PyTorch GroupNorm implementation: The running stats: mean = sum(x) / N, where N = C_g * T (for one group). Variance = sum((x - mean)^2) / N. Then rstd = 1 / sqrt(variance + eps). Yes, it's the population variance over the group, not sample variance. So denominator is C_g * T. After computing mean and rstd (1/sqrt(var+eps)), we apply normalization. We need gamma and beta if affine. gamma and beta are per output channel: shape (out_channels,). So for output channel c_out, we read gamma[c_out] and beta[c_out]. We can store gamma and beta in shared memory or registers. Since each warp handles one channel, we can load gamma and beta for that channel into registers. But after we compute mean and var (shared across block), each thread normalizes its assigned elements. For thread in warp_id, lane_id, for each t it handles (similar loop as conv), it reads smem[warp_id * T + t], computes (val - mean) * rstd, multiplies by gamma, adds beta, and writes to global output. We need to be careful about writing output to global memory in coalesced manner. Output layout: (N, C_out, T_out). So for output channel c_out, time t, the address is n*C_out*T_out + c_out*T_out + t. Since threads in a warp handle contiguous t for same c_out, writing is coalesced. Great. Potential issues: - Since we need to load x for conv, x is in global memory. We need to pass pointers and dimensions. - We also need to handle cases where C_g * T > shared memory capacity? Let's check. Max shared memory per block on modern GPUs (A100, H100) is up to 164KB or 228KB, but default is 48KB or 100KB. C_g * T floats = (out_channels/num_groups) * T_out * 4 bytes. With out_channels up to maybe 512, groups 32, T up to maybe 1024 or 2048. 512/32=16, 16*1024*4=64KB. That's close to 48KB but might still work if we use dynamic shared memory and set max shared memory. However, to be safe, we might want to limit shared memory usage or check the GPU specs. Let's get the GPU specs to know the SM count and shared memory per SM.

I think I should implement a two-pass kernel and test it. If it's too slow due to double compute, I can try a single-pass with more shared memory. Let me draft the kernel: ```cuda __global__ void fused_conv1d_groupnorm( const float* __restrict__ x, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ gamma, const float* __restrict__ beta, float* __restrict__ y, int N, int C_in, int C_out, int T_in, int T_out, int num_groups, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, float eps ) { int n = blockIdx.x; int g = blockIdx.y; int channels_per_group = C_out / num_groups; int c_start = g * channels_per_group; // Weights in shared memory: channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size extern __shared__ float shared[]; float* w_shared = shared; // Load weights for this group int w_size = channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size; for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < w_size; i += blockDim.x) { int kw = i % kernel_size; int ci = (i / kernel_size) % C_in; int co = i / (kernel_size * C_in); w_shared[i] = weight[(c_start + co) * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + kw]; } __syncthreads(); // Each warp handles one output channel int warp_id = threadIdx.x / 32; int lane_id = threadIdx.x % 32; int num_warps = blockDim.x / 32; // First pass: compute conv and accumulate stats float local_sum = 0.0f; float local_sum_sq = 0.0f; for (int tile = 0; tile < T_out; tile += 32) { // Each thread in warp handles one time position within the tile // and iterates over 32 different time blocks // Actually, let's have each warp process 32 consecutive times // Warp w, lane j processes: time = tile + j for one iteration // But then we'd need T_out/32 tiles. For T_out=1024, that's 32 tiles. // Wait, we said each warp handles all 1024 times with 32 iterations of 32 times each. // So there are 32 iterations total, not T_out/32 tiles. for (int iter = 0; iter < 32; iter++) { int t = iter * 32 + lane_id; if (t >= T_out) continue; // Compute conv for time t, channel c_start + warp_id float acc = 0.0f; for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { for (int k = 0; k < kernel_size; k++) { int t_in = t * stride + k * dilation - padding; float xval = 0.0f; if (t_in >= 0 && t_in < T_in) { xval = x[n * C_in * T_in + ci * T_in + t_in]; } float wval = w_shared[warp_id * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + k]; acc += xval * wval; } } local_sum += acc; local_sum_sq += acc * acc; } } // Warp reduce for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { local_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum, offset); local_sum_sq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum_sq, offset); } // Block reduce using shared memory if (lane_id == 0) { w_shared[warp_id] = local_sum; // Reuse weight shared memory! We're done with weights. w_shared[warp_id + num_warps] = local_sum_sq; } __syncthreads(); if (threadIdx.x == 0) { float group_sum = 0.0f, group_sum_sq = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < num_warps; i++) { group_sum += w_shared[i]; group_sum_sq += w_shared[i + num_warps]; } float count = (float)(channels_per_group * T_out); float mean = group_sum / count; float var = group_sum_sq / count - mean * mean; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + eps); w_shared[0] = mean; w_shared[1] = inv_std; } __syncthreads(); float mean = w_shared[0]; float inv_std = w_shared[1]; // Second pass: recompute, normalize, write // But we need gamma/beta for each channel for (int iter = 0; iter < 32; iter++) { int t = iter * 32 + lane_id; if (t >= T_out) continue; float acc = 0.0f; for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { for (int k = 0; k < kernel_size; k++) { int t_in = t * stride + k * dilation - padding; float xval = 0.0f; if (t_in >= 0 && t_in < T_in) { xval = x[n * C_in * T_in + ci * T_in + t_in]; } float wval = w_shared[original memory location]; // Wait, we overwrote weights! } } } } ``` Oops, we overwrote the weights in the block reduce! That's a problem. We need to keep weights for the second pass. Options: 1. Redo the block reduction using different shared memory 2. Reload weights from global memory in pass 2 3. Use a separate shared memory array for stats Since weights are 12KB and stats need only a few floats, we can just use a different part of shared memory. Or use a fixed-size array for stats. Now let me draft the CUDA code. I'll need to handle: - The `extern "C"` wrapper function for pybind - The kernel itself - The Python `ModelNew` class I also need to make sure I handle the affine GroupNorm parameters: gamma and beta are per-channel. Let me write the kernel: ```cuda __global__ void fused_conv1d_groupnorm_kernel( const float* __restrict__ x, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ gamma, const float* __restrict__ beta, float* __restrict__ y, int N, int C_in, int C_out, int T_in, int T_out, int num_groups, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, float eps, bool affine ) { int n = blockIdx.x; int g = blockIdx.y; int channels_per_group = C_out / num_groups; int c_start = g * channels_per_group; // Number of warps per block: 512 / 32 = 16 const int WARPS_PER_BLOCK = 16; const int THREADS_PER_WARP = 32; int warp_id = threadIdx.x / THREADS_PER_WARP; int lane_id = threadIdx.x % THREADS_PER_WARP; int out_c = c_start + warp_id / 2; // 0..7 int time_half = warp_id % 2; // 0 or 1 // Shared memory for weights: channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size extern __shared__ float sdata[]; float* w_shared = sdata; int w_total = channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size; // Load weights cooperatively for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < w_total; i += blockDim.x) { int kw = i % kernel_size; int ci = (i / kernel_size) % C_in; int co = i / (kernel_size * C_in); w_shared[i] = weight[(c_start + co) * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + kw]; } __syncthreads(); // Register storage for computed outputs float out_vals[16]; // 16 iterations * 1 output per iteration float local_sum = 0.0f; float local_sum_sq = 0.0f; // First pass: compute conv and accumulate stats #pragma unroll for (int iter = 0; iter < 16; iter++) { int t_out = time_half * 512 + iter * 32 + lane_id; float acc = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { #pragma unroll for (int k = 0; k < kernel_size; k++) { int t_in = t_out * stride + k * dilation - padding; float xval = 0.0f; if (t_in >= 0 && t_in < T_in) { xval = x[((n * C_in + ci) * T_in) + t_in]; } float wval = w_shared[(warp_id / 2) * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + k]; acc += xval * wval; } } out_vals[iter] = acc; local_sum += acc; local_sum_sq += acc * acc; } // Warp reduce sum and sum_sq for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { local_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum, offset); local_sum_sq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum_sq, offset); } // Store warp results to shared memory (we can overwrite weights now) if (lane_id == 0) { w_shared[warp_id] = local_sum; w_shared[WARPS_PER_BLOCK + warp_id] = local_sum_sq; } __syncthreads(); // Compute group mean and inv_std if (threadIdx.x == 0) { float group_sum = 0.0f; float group_sum_sq = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < WARPS_PER_BLOCK; i++) { group_sum += w_shared[i]; group_sum_sq += w_shared[WARPS_PER_BLOCK + i]; } float count = float(channels_per_group * T_out); float mean = group_sum / count; float var = group_sum_sq / count - mean * mean; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + eps); w_shared[0] = mean; w_shared[1] = inv_std; } __syncthreads(); float mean = w_shared[0]; float inv_std = w_shared[1]; // Normalize, apply affine, and write #pragma unroll for (int iter = 0; iter < 16; iter++) { int t_out = time_half * 512 + iter * 32 + lane_id; float val = (out_vals[iter] - mean) * inv_std; if (affine) { val = val * gamma[out_c] + beta[out_c]; } y[((n * C_out + out_c) * T_out) + t_out] = val; } } ``` Wait, I see a potential issue. Wait, consecutive threads j write to consecutive addresses. This is a coalesced shared memory write. No bank conflicts. The kernel will compute: - `warps_per_channel = blockDim.x / 32 / channels_per_group` if `blockDim.x / 32 >= channels_per_group`. - If not, we use a fallback. In Python: ```python def forward(self, x): N, C_in, T = x.shape T_out = (T + 2*self.padding - self.dilation*(self.kernel_size-1) - 1) // self.stride + 1 C_pg = self.out_channels // self.num_groups if C_pg <= 16 and self.block_size >= C_pg * 32: # Use fused kernel pass else: # Use separate conv + group norm # But this isn't a try/except fallback, just an if/else out = self.conv(x) out = self.norm(out) return out ``` I'll implement the single-pass fused kernel with 512 threads and shared memory output buffer. Let me write the code: ```cuda __global__ void fused_conv1d_groupnorm_forward( const float* __restrict__ x, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ gamma, const float* __restrict__ beta, float* __restrict__ y, int N, int C_in, int C_out, int T_in, int T_out, int num_groups, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, float eps, bool affine ) { int n = blockIdx.x; int g = blockIdx.y; int channels_per_group = C_out / num_groups; int c_start = g * channels_per_group; int num_warps = blockDim.x / 32; int warp_id = threadIdx.x / 32; int lane_id = threadIdx.x % 32; // Determine warps per channel and time split int warps_per_channel = num_warps / channels_per_group; int channel_idx = warp_id / warps_per_channel; int time_split = warp_id % warps_per_channel; int out_c = c_start + channel_idx; int times_per_warp = T_out / warps_per_channel; int time_start = time_split * times_per_warp; int num_iters = times_per_warp / 32; // Shared memory layout: [weights (C_pg * C_in * K)] [outputs (C_pg * T_out)] [stats (2)] extern __shared__ float sdata[]; float* w_shared = sdata; float* out_shared = sdata + channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size; float* stats_shared = out_shared + channels_per_group * T_out; int w_total = channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size; for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < w_total; i += blockDim.x) { int kw = i % kernel_size; int ci = (i / kernel_size) % C_in; int co = i / (kernel_size * C_in); w_shared[i] = weight[(c_start + co) * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + kw]; } __syncthreads(); float local_sum = 0.0f; float local_sum_sq = 0.0f; // Compute conv outputs and store to shared memory for (int iter = 0; iter < num_iters; iter++) { int t_out = time_start + iter * 32 + lane_id; float acc = 0.0f; for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { for (int k = 0; k < kernel_size; k++) { int t_in = t_out * stride + k * dilation - padding; float xval = 0.0f; if (t_in >= 0 && t_in < T_in) { xval = x[((n * C_in + ci) * T_in) + t_in]; } float wval = w_shared[channel_idx * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + k]; acc += xval * wval; } } int out_idx = channel_idx * T_out + t_out; out_shared[out_idx] = acc; local_sum += acc; local_sum_sq += acc * acc; } // Warp reduce for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { local_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum, offset); local_sum_sq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum_sq, offset); } if (lane_id == 0) { w_shared[warp_id] = local_sum; // Reuse weight memory after conv done w_shared[warp_id + num_warps] = local_sum_sq; } __syncthreads(); if (threadIdx.x == 0) { float group_sum = 0.0f; float group_sum_sq = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < num_warps; i++) { group_sum += w_shared[i]; group_sum_sq += w_shared[num_warps + i]; } float count = float(channels_per_group * T_out); float mean = group_sum / count; float var = group_sum_sq / count - mean * mean; stats_shared[0] = mean; stats_shared[1] = rsqrtf(var + eps); } __syncthreads(); float mean = stats_shared[0]; float inv_std = stats_shared[1]; // Normalize and write float gamma_c = affine ? gamma[out_c] : 1.0f; float beta_c = affine ? beta[out_c] : 0.0f; for (int iter = 0; iter < num_iters; iter++) { int t_out = time_start + iter * 32 + lane_id; float val = out_shared[channel_idx * T_out + t_out]; val = (val - mean) * inv_std; if (affine) { val = val * gamma_c + beta_c; } y[((n * C_out + out_c) * T_out) + t_out] = val; } } ``` Wait, there are several issues: 1. `num_warps / channels_per_group` might not be integer. We should use integer division, but ensure num_warps >= channels_per_group. 2. `T_out / warps_per_channel` might not be integer. For T_out=1024 and warps_per_channel=2, it's 512. Good. Let me draft the complete Python source for ModelNew: ```python import torch import torch.nn as nn from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline CUDA_SOURCE = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> __global__ void fused_conv1d_groupnorm_kernel(...) { ... } torch::Tensor fused_conv1d_groupnorm_forward_cuda( torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor gamma, torch::Tensor beta, int num_groups, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, float eps, bool affine ) { // ... launch kernel ... } ''' class ModelNew(nn.Module): def __init__(self, ...): super().__init__() # ... init params ... self.cuda_ext = load_inline( name="fused_conv1d_groupnorm", cpp_sources=''' torch::Tensor fused_conv1d_groupnorm_forward_cuda(torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor gamma, torch::Tensor beta, int num_groups, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, float eps, bool affine); ''', cuda_sources=CUDA_SOURCE, functions=['fused_conv1d_groupnorm_forward_cuda'], extra_cuda_cflags=['-O3', '--use_fast_math'], verbose=False, ) def forward(self, x): if x.device.type != 'cuda': # CPU fallback - use PyTorch ops ... # Check if config is supported by kernel N, C_in, T = x.shape C_out = self.out_channels T_out = (T + 2 * self.padding - self.dilation * (self.kernel_size - 1) - 1) // self.stride + 1 C_pg = C_out // self.num_groups # Kernel supports channels_per_group <= 16 and divides evenly into 16 warps # Actually, with the channel cycling approach, we can support any C_pg as long as shared memory fits shared_needed = C_pg * C_in * self.kernel_size * 4 + C_pg * T_out * 4 + 34 * 4 if C_pg > 16 or shared_needed > 96 * 1024: # Fallback out = torch.nn.functional.conv1d(x, self.weight, None, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, 1) out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm(out, self.num_groups, self.gamma, self.beta, self.eps) return out return self.cuda_ext.fused_conv1d_groupnorm_forward_cuda( x, self.weight, self.gamma, self.beta, self.num_groups, self.kernel_size, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, self.eps, self.affine ) ``` Wait, I need to extract gamma and beta from the GroupNorm module. Create the parameters directly For matching PyTorch's initialization, it's easiest to create the submodules and extract their parameters: ```python def __init__(self, ...): super().__init__() self.in_channels = in_channels self.out_channels = out_channels self.num_groups = num_groups self.kernel_size = kernel_size self.stride = stride self.padding = padding self.dilation = dilation self.eps = eps self.affine = affine # Create reference modules to get correctly initialized parameters conv = nn.Conv1d(in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size, stride=stride, padding=padding, dilation=dilation, bias=False) norm = nn.GroupNorm(num_groups=num_groups, num_channels=out_channels, eps=eps, affine=affine) self.weight = nn.Parameter(conv.weight.data) if affine: self.gamma = nn.Parameter(norm.weight.data) self.beta = nn.Parameter(norm.bias.data) else: self.register_buffer('gamma', None) self.register_buffer('beta', None) # Also register a dummy buffer to keep Module happy self.register_buffer('_dummy', torch.zeros(1)) self.cuda_ext = load_inline(...) ``` Wait, `self.gamma` and `self.beta` need to exist even if affine=False, for the kernel interface. Let me write the full CUDA kernel carefully: ```cuda #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> __global__ void fused_conv1d_groupnorm_kernel( const float* __restrict__ x, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ gamma, const float* __restrict__ beta, float* __restrict__ y, int N, int C_in, int C_out, int T_in, int T_out, int num_groups, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, float eps, bool affine ) { int n = blockIdx.x; int g = blockIdx.y; int channels_per_group = C_out / num_groups; int c_start = g * channels_per_group; int num_warps = blockDim.x / 32; int warp_id = threadIdx.x / 32; int lane_id = threadIdx.x % 32; // Determine channel assignment for this warp int channel_idx = warp_id; // 0..num_warps-1 int out_c = c_start + channel_idx; // If this warp doesn't have a valid channel, participate in reduction but don't compute bool has_work = (channel_idx < channels_per_group); // Shared memory layout extern __shared__ float sdata[]; float* w_shared = sdata; float* out_shared = sdata + channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size; float* stats_area = out_shared + channels_per_group * T_out; int w_total = channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size; // Load weights cooperatively for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < w_total; i += blockDim.x) { int kw = i % kernel_size; int ci = (i / kernel_size) % C_in; int co = i / (kernel_size * C_in); w_shared[i] = weight[(c_start + co) * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + kw]; } __syncthreads(); float local_sum = 0.0f; float local_sum_sq = 0.0f; if (has_work) { int num_iters = (T_out + 31) / 32; for (int iter = 0; iter < num_iters; iter++) { int t_out = iter * 32 + lane_id; if (t_out >= T_out) continue; float acc = 0.0f; if (kernel_size == 3) { int t_in_base = t_out * stride - padding; #pragma unroll for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { int base_idx = ((n * C_in + ci) * T_in); int w_base = channel_idx * C_in * 3 + ci * 3; int t0 = t_in_base; float x0 = (t0 >= 0 && t0 < T_in) ? x[base_idx + t0] : 0.0f; acc += x0 * w_shared[w_base + 0]; int t1 = t_in_base + dilation; float x1 = (t1 >= 0 && t1 < T_in) ? x[base_idx + t1] : 0.0f; acc += x1 * w_shared[w_base + 1]; int t2 = t_in_base + 2 * dilation; float x2 = (t2 >= 0 && t2 < T_in) ? x[base_idx + t2] : 0.0f; acc += x2 * w_shared[w_base + 2]; } } else { for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { for (int k = 0; k < kernel_size; k++) { int t_in = t_out * stride + k * dilation - padding; float xval = 0.0f; if (t_in >= 0 && t_in < T_in) { xval = x[((n * C_in + ci) * T_in) + t_in]; } float wval = w_shared[channel_idx * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + k]; acc += xval * wval; } } } out_shared[channel_idx * T_out + t_out] = acc; local_sum += acc; local_sum_sq += acc * acc; } } // Warp reduction for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { local_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum, offset); local_sum_sq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum_sq, offset); } // Write warp results to shared memory if (lane_id == 0) { stats_area[warp_id] = local_sum; stats_area[warp_id + num_warps] = local_sum_sq; } __syncthreads(); // Compute group statistics if (threadIdx.x == 0) { float group_sum = 0.0f; float group_sum_sq = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < num_warps; i++) { group_sum += stats_area[i]; group_sum_sq += stats_area[i + num_warps]; } float count = float(channels_per_group * T_out); float mean = group_sum / count; float var = group_sum_sq / count - mean * mean; stats_area[2 * num_warps] = mean; stats_area[2 * num_warps + 1] = rsqrtf(var + eps); } __syncthreads(); float mean = stats_area[2 * num_warps]; float inv_std = stats_area[2 * num_warps + 1]; // Normalize and write output if (has_work) { float gamma_c = affine ? gamma[out_c] : 1.0f; float beta_c = affine ? beta[out_c] : 0.0f; int num_iters = (T_out + 31) / 32; for (int iter = 0; iter < num_iters; iter++) { int t_out = iter * 32 + lane_id; if (t_out >= T_out) continue; float val = out_shared[channel_idx * T_out + t_out]; val = (val - mean) * inv_std; if (affine) { val = val * gamma_c + beta_c; } y[((n * C_out + out_c) * T_out) + t_out] = val; } } } ``` Wait, this has an issue. With 16 warps and only 8 channels, 8 warps will have `has_work = false`. Their `local_sum` and `local_sum_sq` will be 0. That's fine - they contribute 0 to the group stats. Let me add a clean fallback: ```python def forward(self, x): if not x.is_cuda: # CPU fallback out = torch.nn.functional.conv1d(x, self.weight, None, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, 1) if self.affine: out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm(out, self.num_groups, self.gamma, self.beta, self.eps) else: out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm(out, self.num_groups, None, None, self.eps) return out N, C_in, T = x.shape C_out = self.out_channels T_out = (T + 2 * self.padding - self.dilation * (self.kernel_size - 1) - 1) // self.stride + 1 C_pg = C_out // self.num_groups # Check if our optimized kernel can handle this max_warps = 16 # Since we use 512 threads shared_needed = C_pg * C_in * self.kernel_size * 4 + C_pg * T_out * 4 + (max_warps * 2 + 2) * 4 if C_pg > max_warps or shared_needed > 96 * 1024 or T_out <= 0: # Config not supported by kernel, use PyTorch fallback out = torch.nn.functional.conv1d(x, self.weight, None, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, 1) if self.affine: out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm(out, self.num_groups, self.gamma, self.beta, self.eps) else: out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm(out, self.num_groups, None, None, self.eps) return out gamma = self.gamma if self.affine else torch.empty(0, device=x.device, dtype=x.dtype) beta = self.beta if self.affine else torch.empty(0, device=x.device, dtype=x.dtype) return self.cuda_ext.fused_conv1d_groupnorm_forward_cuda( x, self.weight, gamma, beta, self.num_groups, self.kernel_size, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, self.eps, self.affine ) ``` This looks clean and doesn't use try/except. But first, let me reconsider if there's a simpler kernel that avoids shared memory for outputs by using registers. I already calculated that with 512 threads and 16 warps, for C_pg=8, each warp handles 512 times, which means 16 iterations, and each thread stores 16 outputs. That's 16 floats = 16 registers. With other registers, maybe 25-30 total. At 4 blocks per SM and 512 threads each = 2048 threads, each thread can use up to floor(64K / 2048) = 32 registers. So 25-30 is feasible! If the compiler successfully keeps the 16 outputs in registers, we can eliminate the 32KB output buffer. This would reduce shared memory to 12KB + 136B = 12.2KB. And we'd be safe from register spilling if the compiler cooperates. How can I help the compiler? By declaring the array as `float out_vals[16];` and using it in a structured way. But the issue is that the write and read are separated by syncthreads and other logic. The compiler might still be able to keep them in registers since they're local to each thread and accessed sequentially. Let me try both approaches. I'll write the kernel with register storage and see if it compiles and runs correctly. If register spilling occurs, the performance will degrade, and I can switch to shared memory. Actually, you know what, I'll use shared memory for outputs since it's more reliable. The performance difference might not be huge. Wait, actually, I just thought of a better register trick. Instead of storing ALL outputs, each thread can store outputs in a 16-element array. After the conv loop, the thread has all 16 outputs. Then we can compute the local sum and sum_sq directly from the array. Then do warp shuffle reduction. Then syncthreads, compute mean/var. Then normalize the 16 outputs and write to global memory. No need for shared memory output buffer! This uses only 16 registers per thread for `out_vals`, plus a few for loops. Let's estimate: - out_vals[16] = 16 registers - acc = 1 - local_sum = 1 - local_sum_sq = 1 - mean, inv_std, gamma_c, beta_c = 4 - loop indices = 2 - temporary for indexing = 2 Total: ~27 registers. Under 32! We should be good. And shared memory is ONLY needed for weights (12KB) and stats reduction (small). Total ~12.2KB. With 512 threads = 4 blocks per SM (thread-limited). 12.2KB * 4 = 48.8KB. Fine. This is much better! Let me rewrite the kernel to use registers. Wait, I need to make sure that `out_vals[16]` doesn't get spilled. The compiler has to keep it live across the syncthreads and stats computation. Since we're accessing it sequentially in the second loop, and the values are independent, the compiler should be able to keep them in registers. However, there's a subtlety. For the warp shuffle reduction, we're reducing `local_sum` and `local_sum_sq`, not `out_vals`. The `out_vals` are only used in the final write loop. Between the conv loop and the write loop, there's about 10-20 instructions (reduction, syncthreads, stats computation, syncthreads). The compiler should keep `out_vals` in registers during this time. Let me write this version: ```cuda __global__ void fused_conv1d_groupnorm_kernel( const float* __restrict__ x, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ gamma, const float* __restrict__ beta, float* __restrict__ y, int N, int C_in, int C_out, int T_in, int T_out, int num_groups, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, float eps, bool affine ) { int n = blockIdx.x; int g = blockIdx.y; int channels_per_group = C_out / num_groups; int c_start = g * channels_per_group; int num_warps = blockDim.x / 32; int warp_id = threadIdx.x / 32; int lane_id = threadIdx.x % 32; int channel_idx = warp_id; int out_c = c_start + channel_idx; bool has_work = (channel_idx < channels_per_group); extern __shared__ float sdata[]; float* w_shared = sdata; float* stats_area = w_shared + channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size; int w_total = channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size; for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < w_total; i += blockDim.x) { int kw = i % kernel_size; int ci = (i / kernel_size) % C_in; int co = i / (kernel_size * C_in); w_shared[i] = weight[(c_start + co) * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + kw]; } __syncthreads(); // Each thread computes a tile of times for its channel // With 512 threads (16 warps), C_pg=8, each warp handles 512 times // 512 / 32 = 16 iterations per thread float out_vals[16]; float local_sum = 0.0f; float local_sum_sq = 0.0f; if (has_work) { int num_iters = (T_out + 31) / 32; if (num_iters > 16) num_iters = 16; // Safety for our array size for (int iter = 0; iter < num_iters; iter++) { int t_out = iter * 32 + lane_id; if (t_out >= T_out) { out_vals[iter] = 0.0f; continue; } float acc = 0.0f; // Unrolled kernel_size=3 path if (kernel_size == 3) { int t_in_base = t_out * stride - padding; #pragma unroll for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { int base_idx = ((n * C_in + ci) * T_in); int w_base = channel_idx * C_in * 3 + ci * 3; int t0 = t_in_base; float x0 = (t0 >= 0 && t0 < T_in) ? x[base_idx + t0] : 0.0f; acc += x0 * w_shared[w_base + 0]; int t1 = t_in_base + dilation; float x1 = (t1 >= 0 && t1 < T_in) ? x[base_idx + t1] : 0.0f; acc += x1 * w_shared[w_base + 1]; int t2 = t_in_base + 2 * dilation; float x2 = (t2 >= 0 && t2 < T_in) ? x[base_idx + t2] : 0.0f; acc += x2 * w_shared[w_base + 2]; } } else { for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { #pragma unroll for (int k = 0; k < kernel_size; k++) { int t_in = t_out * stride + k * dilation - padding; float xval = 0.0f; if (t_in >= 0 && t_in < T_in) { xval = x[((n * C_in + ci) * T_in) + t_in]; } acc += xval * w_shared[channel_idx * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + k]; } } } out_vals[iter] = acc; local_sum += acc; local_sum_sq += acc * acc; } // Pad remaining iterations if T_out < 512 for (int iter = num_iters; iter < 16; iter++) { out_vals[iter] = 0.0f; } } else { #pragma unroll for (int iter = 0; iter < 16; iter++) { out_vals[iter] = 0.0f; } } // Warp reduction for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { local_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum, offset); local_sum_sq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum_sq, offset); } if (lane_id == 0) { stats_area[warp_id] = local_sum; stats_area[warp_id + num_warps] = local_sum_sq; } __syncthreads(); if (threadIdx.x == 0) { float group_sum = 0.0f; float group_sum_sq = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < num_warps; i++) { group_sum += stats_area[i]; group_sum_sq += stats_area[i + num_warps]; } float count = float(channels_per_group * T_out); float mean = group_sum / count; float var = group_sum_sq / count - mean * mean; stats_area[2 * num_warps] = mean; stats_area[2 * num_warps + 1] = rsqrtf(var + eps); } __syncthreads(); float mean = stats_area[2 * num_warps]; float inv_std = stats_area[2 * num_warps + 1]; if (has_work) { float gamma_c = affine ? gamma[out_c] : 1.0f; float beta_c = affine ? beta[out_c] : 0.0f; int num_iters = (T_out + 31) / 32; if (num_iters > 16) num_iters = 16; for (int iter = 0; iter < num_iters; iter++) { int t_out = iter * 32 + lane_id; if (t_out >= T_out) continue; float val = out_vals[iter]; val = (val - mean) * inv_std; if (affine) { val = val * gamma_c + beta_c; } y[((n * C_out + out_c) * T_out) + t_out] = val; } } } ``` Wait, there are several issues with this register-based approach: 1. `out_vals[16]` assumes `num_iters <= 16`. For T_out=1024 with 512 threads and C_pg=8, num_iters = 16. Good. But if T_out > 512 (like 2048), we'd need 32 iterations and `out_vals[32]`, which might spill. 2. For C_pg=16 with 512 threads, warps_per_channel=1, each warp handles 1024 times, num_iters=32. We'd need `out_vals[32]`. Register pressure: 32 + ~10 = 42 registers. At 4 blocks per SM (512 threads = 2048 threads), limit is 32 registers. Spilling! 3. For C_pg=4 with 512 threads, warps_per_channel=4, each warp handles 256 times, num_iters=8. `out_vals[8]`. Easy. So the register approach works for small `num_iters` but not for large ones. For the default case with C_pg=8 and T_out=1024, num_iters=16. This should fit in 32 registers (16 for out_vals + ~10 for other variables = 26). But if we want to support the general case where num_iters could be up to 32, register spilling is likely. So shared memory for outputs is safer. Hmm, let me compromise. I'll use shared memory for outputs in a general kernel that handles all cases where the output buffer fits. For cases where it doesn't fit, I'll fall back to PyTorch ops. This covers the common case perfectly. Actually, let me just use the shared memory approach. It's simpler and more robust. On H100, shared memory is 228KB per SM. With 44KB per block, 228 / 44 = 5.18. So we can run 5 blocks per SM if threads allow. But with 512 threads, max is 4 blocks per SM (2048 / 512 = 4). Let me finalize the code. Actually, before that, let me consider one more optimization: split the time dimension processing to use vector loads for input. For K=3, stride=1, dilation=1, each thread needs input at t-1, t, t+1. With 32 threads in a warp, we need times base-1 to base+32. That's 34 consecutive floats. Instead of each thread loading independently, the warp could load shared data cooperatively. But we're not using shared memory for input. With 16 warps loading the same input, L1 cache should help. And global memory loads are coalesced (each thread loads 3 floats at different offsets). Actually, let me check coalescing for the general loop: ```cuda for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { for (int k = 0; k < kernel_size; k++) { int t_in = t_out * stride + k * dilation - padding; float xval = (t_in >= 0 && t_in < T_in) ? x[((n * C_in + ci) * T_in) + t_in] : 0.0f; ... } } ``` In iteration i of the outermost time loop: - Thread j has t_out = i * 32 + j (approximately) - For fixed ci and k, thread j accesses x[n, ci, t_out * stride + k * dilation - padding] - If stride=1 and dilation=1, thread j accesses x[n, ci, i*32 + j + k - 1] - Consecutive threads access consecutive addresses. COALESCED! Good. For the K=3 unrolled path: - Thread j accesses x[n, ci, i*32 + j - 1], x[n, ci, i*32 + j], x[n, ci, i*32 + j + 1] - Each of these is a separate load instruction, but they're all coalesced within the warp. Actually, there's an opportunity: instead of 3 separate loads per ci, we can load them as a float3 or with 128-bit loads where possible. But this is getting into micro-optimization. Let me keep it simple. Wait, for the K=3 path with t_in_base = i*32 + j - 1: - t0 = i*32 + j - 1 - t1 = i*32 + j - t2 = i*32 + j + 1 Thread j loads x[base + j - 1], x[base + j], x[base + j + 1] where base = i*32. The loads at base + j are perfectly coalesced. The loads at base + j - 1 are also coalesced (just offset by 1). The loads at base + j + 1 are coalesced too. The compiler might even merge some of these loads. I think this is good enough. Now let me think about one more thing. In the K=3 unrolled path, I compute `t0`, `t1`, `t2` and then branch on each one. With K=3 and 128 channels, that's 384 branches per thread. Since most threads in the warp take the same branch (except at tile boundaries), the divergence is minimal. But it's still many branch instructions. For the default case (padding=1, T_out=T_in=1024), only the first iteration (t_out near 0) and last iteration (t_out near 1023) have any divergence. For middle iterations, all 3 loads are valid for all threads. The compiler might be smart enough to optimize this. But with explicit bounds checks inside the inner loop, we're adding branches. I can hoist the bounds check outside: For a warp processing times [time_start, time_end): - In most iterations, all times are valid (not near boundaries) - Only the first and last iterations might touch boundaries I can handle this by having special cases for boundary iterations. Actually, let me also handle the case where the kernel isn't called with exactly the expected block size. Currently I hardcoded some assumptions. Let me make it robust. Actually, for simplicity, I'll write the kernel to work with any block size that's a multiple of 32. The key is: - `num_warps = blockDim.x / 32` - `channel_idx = warp_id % channels_per_group` (cycle through channels) - Each warp processes all times for its assigned channel Wait, if channel_idx cycles and multiple warps process the same channel, they all process the SAME times. That's duplicate work! I need to partition times among warps processing the same channel. If `warps_per_channel = num_warps / channels_per_group` (integer division), then each channel gets that many warps, and times are partitioned. But this requires `num_warps % channels_per_group == 0` for equal distribution. If `num_warps = 16` and `channels_per_group = 12`, then `warps_per_channel = 1` with remainder 4. So 4 channels get 2 warps and 8 channels get 1 warp. Unequal. To avoid complexity, I'll require `channels_per_group <= num_warps` and `num_warps % channels_per_group == 0`. This is checked in Python before launching. For invalid configs, fallback to PyTorch ops. For valid configs: - `warps_per_channel = num_warps / channels_per_group` - Each warp handles `T_out / warps_per_channel` times (must divide evenly, or use min/max) To keep it simple, I'll also require that `T_out % warps_per_channel == 0`. If not, fallback. For the default case: C_pg=8, num_warps=16 (block=512), warps_per_channel=2, T_out=1024, 1024 % 2 = 0. Good. OK I'll write the final code now. ```python import torch import torch.nn as nn from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline CUDA_SOURCE = """ #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> __global__ void fused_conv1d_groupnorm_kernel( const float* __restrict__ x, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ gamma, const float* __restrict__ beta, float* __restrict__ y, int N, int C_in, int C_out, int T_in, int T_out, int num_groups, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, float eps, bool affine ) { int n = blockIdx.x; int g = blockIdx.y; int channels_per_group = C_out / num_groups; int c_start = g * channels_per_group; int num_warps = blockDim.x / 32; int warp_id = threadIdx.x / 32; int lane_id = threadIdx.x % 32; // Each warp handles one channel; if more warps than channels, some are idle int channel_idx = warp_id; int out_c = c_start + channel_idx; bool has_work = (channel_idx < channels_per_group); // Partition times among warps handling the same channel int warps_per_channel = num_warps / channels_per_group; int warp_in_channel = warp_id % warps_per_channel; int times_per_warp = (T_out + warps_per_channel - 1) / warps_per_channel; int time_start = warp_in_channel * times_per_warp; int time_end = min(time_start + times_per_warp, T_out); int actual_times = time_end - time_start; int num_iters = (actual_times + 31) / 32; // Shared memory layout: [weights] [outputs] [stats] extern __shared__ float sdata[]; float* w_shared = sdata; float* out_shared = sdata + channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size; float* stats_area = out_shared + channels_per_group * T_out; // Load weights for this group int w_total = channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size; for (int i = threadIdx.x; i < w_total; i += blockDim.x) { int kw = i % kernel_size; int ci = (i / kernel_size) % C_in; int co = i / (kernel_size * C_in); w_shared[i] = weight[(c_start + co) * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + kw]; } __syncthreads(); float local_sum = 0.0f; float local_sum_sq = 0.0f; // Compute conv outputs and store to shared memory if (has_work) { for (int iter = 0; iter < num_iters; iter++) { int t_out = time_start + iter * 32 + lane_id; if (t_out >= time_end) continue; float acc = 0.0f; if (kernel_size == 3) { int t_in_base = t_out * stride - padding; #pragma unroll for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { int base_idx = ((n * C_in + ci) * T_in); int w_base = channel_idx * C_in * 3 + ci * 3; int t0 = t_in_base; float x0 = (t0 >= 0 && t0 < T_in) ? x[base_idx + t0] : 0.0f; acc += x0 * w_shared[w_base + 0]; int t1 = t_in_base + dilation; float x1 = (t1 >= 0 && t1 < T_in) ? x[base_idx + t1] : 0.0f; acc += x1 * w_shared[w_base + 1]; int t2 = t_in_base + 2 * dilation; float x2 = (t2 >= 0 && t2 < T_in) ? x[base_idx + t2] : 0.0f; acc += x2 * w_shared[w_base + 2]; } } else { for (int ci = 0; ci < C_in; ci++) { #pragma unroll 4 for (int k = 0; k < kernel_size; k++) { int t_in = t_out * stride + k * dilation - padding; float xval = 0.0f; if (t_in >= 0 && t_in < T_in) { xval = x[((n * C_in + ci) * T_in) + t_in]; } acc += xval * w_shared[channel_idx * C_in * kernel_size + ci * kernel_size + k]; } } } out_shared[channel_idx * T_out + t_out] = acc; local_sum += acc; local_sum_sq += acc * acc; } } // Warp reduction for sum and sum_sq for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { local_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum, offset); local_sum_sq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, local_sum_sq, offset); } if (lane_id == 0) { stats_area[warp_id] = local_sum; stats_area[warp_id + num_warps] = local_sum_sq; } __syncthreads(); // Compute group statistics if (threadIdx.x == 0) { float group_sum = 0.0f; float group_sum_sq = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < num_warps; i++) { group_sum += stats_area[i]; group_sum_sq += stats_area[i + num_warps]; } float count = float(channels_per_group * T_out); float mean = group_sum / count; float var = group_sum_sq / count - mean * mean; stats_area[2 * num_warps] = mean; stats_area[2 * num_warps + 1] = rsqrtf(var + eps); } __syncthreads(); float mean = stats_area[2 * num_warps]; float inv_std = stats_area[2 * num_warps + 1]; // Normalize and write output if (has_work) { float gamma_c = affine ? gamma[out_c] : 1.0f; float beta_c = affine ? beta[out_c] : 0.0f; for (int iter = 0; iter < num_iters; iter++) { int t_out = time_start + iter * 32 + lane_id; if (t_out >= time_end) continue; float val = out_shared[channel_idx * T_out + t_out]; val = (val - mean) * inv_std; if (affine) { val = val * gamma_c + beta_c; } y[((n * C_out + out_c) * T_out) + t_out] = val; } } } torch::Tensor fused_conv1d_groupnorm_forward_cuda( torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor gamma, torch::Tensor beta, int num_groups, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, float eps, bool affine ) { int N = x.size(0); int C_in = x.size(1); int T_in = x.size(2); int C_out = weight.size(0); int T_out = (T_in + 2 * padding - dilation * (kernel_size - 1) - 1) / stride + 1; auto y = torch::empty({N, C_out, T_out}, x.options()); dim3 grid(N, num_groups); dim3 block(512); int channels_per_group = C_out / num_groups; size_t shared_mem = channels_per_group * C_in * kernel_size * sizeof(float) + channels_per_group * T_out * sizeof(float) + (512 / 32 * 2 + 2) * sizeof(float); const float* gamma_ptr = affine ? gamma.data_ptr<float>() : nullptr; const float* beta_ptr = affine ? beta.data_ptr<float>() : nullptr; fused_conv1d_groupnorm_kernel<<<grid, block, shared_mem, at::cuda::getCurrentCUDAStream()>>>( x.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), gamma_ptr, beta_ptr, y.data_ptr<float>(), N, C_in, C_out, T_in, T_out, num_groups, kernel_size, stride, padding, dilation, eps, affine ); return y; } """ CPP_SOURCES = """ torch::Tensor fused_conv1d_groupnorm_forward_cuda( torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor gamma, torch::Tensor beta, int num_groups, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, float eps, bool affine ); """ class ModelNew(nn.Module): def __init__( self, in_channels: int, out_channels: int, num_groups: int, kernel_size: int = 3, stride: int = 1, self.weight = nn.Parameter(conv.weight.data) if affine: self.gamma = nn.Parameter(norm.weight.data) self.beta = nn.Parameter(norm.bias.data) else: self.gamma = None self.beta = None self.cuda_ext = verbose=False, ) def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor: # Device and shape checks if x.device.type != "cuda": out = torch.nn.functional.conv1d( x, self.weight, None, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, 1 ) if self.affine: out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm( out, self.num_groups, self.gamma, self.beta, self.eps ) else: out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm( out, self.num_groups, None, None, self.eps ) return out N, C_in, T = x.shape C_out = self.out_channels C_pg = C_out // self.num_groups T_out = ( T + 2 * self.padding - self.dilation * (self.kernel_size - 1) - 1 ) // self.stride + 1 # Check if our fast path can handle this config # We use 512 threads = 16 warps max_warps = 16 shared_needed = ( C_pg * C_in * self.kernel_size * 4 + C_pg * T_out * 4 + (max_warps * 2 + 2) * 4 ) if C_pg > max_warps or shared_needed > 96 * 1024 or T_out <= 0: out = torch.nn.functional.conv1d( x, self.weight, None, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, 1 ) if self.affine: out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm( out, self.num_groups, self.gamma, self.beta, self.eps ) else: out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm( out, self.num_groups, None, None, self.eps ) return out if self.affine: gamma = self.gamma beta = self.beta else: gamma = torch.empty(0, device=x.device, dtype=x.dtype) beta = torch.empty(0, device=x.device, dtype=x.dtype) return self.cuda_ext.fused_conv1d_groupnorm_forward_cuda( x, self.weight, gamma, beta, self.num_groups, self.kernel_size, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, self.eps, self.affine ) ``` This looks All covered! This is robust. The only constraint is `channels_per_group <= num_warps`. Now, `num_warps` depends on the block size. With block=512, num_warps=16. With block=256, num_warps=8. I'll use block=512 since it allows up to C_pg=16. But I should also check if exceeding C_pg * T_out * 4 causes shared memory issues. For C_pg=16, T_out=1024: 64KB outputs + weights. + stats = ~76KB. At 4 blocks per SM = 304KB. Still under 228KB? No, 304KB > 228KB! So for C_pg=16, shared memory might be the limiting factor. With 76KB per block, 228 / 76 = 3 blocks per SM. Threads: 4 * 512 = 2048. But shared memory limits to 3 blocks. So 3 * 512 = 1536 threads per SM. 75% occupancy. Still decent. For C_pg=8: 44KB. 228 / 44 = 5.18. Thread limit: 4. So threads are the bottleneck. I just realized: H100 shared memory might not be as straightforward. There are different shared memory configurations. But 228KB is the maximum per block and per SM in the maximum configuration. I think for H100, 228KB is available. Let me compute for C_pg=16, C_in=128, K=3, T_out=1024: - weights: 16 * 128 * 3 * 4 = 24,576 bytes = 24KB - outputs: 16 * 1024 * 4 = 65,536 bytes = 64KB - stats: (16 * 2 + 2) * 4 = 136 bytes = 0.1KB - Total: 88.7KB At 88.7KB per block, with 4 blocks per SM (thread limit): 354.8KB > 228KB. So shared memory limits us to 2 blocks per SM (177.4KB). Then thread occupancy is 2 * 512 = 1024 threads per SM = 50%. For the default case (C_pg=8): 44KB. 4 blocks = 176KB < 228KB. Thread limited to 4 blocks. 100% thread occupancy. Good. If the test uses C_pg > 8, performance might degrade due to lower occupancy. But our kernel is still correct and likely competitive. One more check: with C_pg=8, C_in=128, K=3, T_out=1024, block=512: - Total outputs: 8 * 1024 * 4 = 32KB - weights: 12KB - stats: ~0.1KB - Total shared: 44.1KB - Concurrent blocks: min(4, floor(228/44.1)) = min(4, 5) = 4 - Total waves for 512 blocks: 512 / (132 * 4) = 0.97. Perfect! This should give excellent performance for the default config. Let me refine the code one more time and then submit it for compilation. Actually, I want to handle block=256 as well. If shared memory is tight, 256 threads uses less shared memory for stats (8 warps * 2 + 2 = 18 floats vs 34 floats), but allows 8 blocks per SM. However, 8 blocks per SM with 256 threads = 2048 threads, which is 100% thread occupancy. But we only have 512 blocks total. 512 / (132 * 8) = 0.48 waves. So roughly half the SMs would be busy on the second half. Not as good as 512 threads. Actually, let me just always use 512 threads. The code is written for it. One issue: `stats_area` indexing. I use `stats_area[warp_id]` where warp_id ranges 0..15. And `stats_area[warp_id + num_warps]` where num_warps = 16. So stats_area needs 32 floats. Plus 2 for mean and inv_std. Total 34 floats. In the shared memory size calculation: `(512 / 32 * 2 + 2) * sizeof(float)` = (16 * 2 + 2) * 4 = 136 bytes. Good. Now one subtle bug: in the host size calculation, I computed `shared_mem` but didn't check if it exceeds the limit. The kernel launch will succeed but might run with fewer concurrent blocks. Another potential bug: when `gamma_ptr` or `beta_ptr` is nullptr and `affine` is true, the kernel dereferences them. But `affine` being true means gamma and beta tensors were provided. In Python, if `self.affine` is true, `gamma` and `beta` are nn.Parameter objects with valid data. But wait, in the wrapper, I used: ```cpp const float* gamma_ptr = affine ? gamma.data_ptr<float>() : nullptr; ``` If `gamma` is an empty tensor but `affine` is true, `gamma.data_ptr<float>()` might be nullptr or invalid. But in Python, `self.gamma` is always valid when `self.affine` is true. `torch.empty(0)` is only passed when `affine` is false. So we're good. Let me compile and test now. Actually, I realize I should also think about potential illegal memory accesses. 1. `out_shared[channel_idx * T_out + t_out]`: channel_idx < channels_per_group, t_out < T_out. So index < channels_per_group * T_out. This is within the allocated size. Good. 2. `y[((n * C_out + out_c) * T_out) + t_out]`: n < N, out_c < C_out, t_out < T_out. Total elements = N * C_out * T_out. This matches `y`'s size. Good. 3. `x[...]` and `weight[...]`: similar bounds. We check t_in bounds for x. For weight, the indices are computed from loop variables which are bounded. Good. 4. `gamma[out_c]` and `beta[out_c]`: out_c < C_out. gamma.size(0) should be C_out if affine. In PyTorch, GroupNorm gamma shape is (num_channels,) = (C_out,). Good. One edge case: when `C_pg > max_warps`, we fallback. But what if `T_out` is very large, causing `shared_needed > 96KB` even with small `C_pg`? The fallback handles it. Now let me create a test script to compile and run.

Since each warp handles one channel, lane 0 handles time 0, lane 1 handles time 1, and lane i handles time t_out = i + 32*k for integer k within T_out. This IS per warp! All threads in the same warp handle the same channel. The T_out values are divided across the 32 lanes in the warp. Since they are coalesced writes and reads, this is good. And I fixed the stats array to have (num_warps * 2 + 2) entries where num_warps = 16. Good. But wait: in v3, I say "bool has_work = (warp_id < channels_per_group);". Warps without work write 0 to stats entry or simply don't write. If I use double for conv accumulation, the dot product would be: acc = 0.0 (double) for each element: acc += xval * weight (xval and weight are float, product is float, added to double with cast) The result would be double-precision conv output. Then when I write to shared memory as float and compute norm, the conv output would be slightly different from PyTorch's fp32 conv. Actually, if I accumulate in float but with the exact same order as PyTorch GEMM... I can't know that order. Anyway, let me just try the custom norm approach. Actually, there's one more thing I want to test: can I keep my fused kernel but instead of computing conv myself, I use PyTorch's conv1d to get the conv output, then feed that into a fused kernel that just does groupnorm but treats it as if it got the conv output? No, that's just separate steps. Let me write a clean groupnorm-only kernel that works on the conv output. Kernel design: - Each block handles one (n, g) - Block size: 256 threads - Each thread iterates over channels in the group and time positions in strided fashion - Uses shared memory for reduction - First pass computes sum and sum_sq in float/double - Second pass reads the input again and normalizes Wait, I can optimize memory by reading once into shared memory if the group data fits. 32KB for 8 channels. With 32 groups and batch 16, total shared peak doesn't matter because it's per block. But actually, for a batch of 16 and 32 groups, I'd launch 16*32=512 blocks. Each block needs ~256 threads and ~40KB shared memory. With 132 SMs and limited shared memory per SM (228KB / 40KB = 5 blocks per SM), that's ~660 concurrent blocks, which is more than 512, so it can run concurrently. Good. But we don't have the conv output stored in shared memory. We'd have to read it from global memory. For the first pass: read global, accumulate. For second pass: read global, normalize, write global. That's 2 reads + 1 write. PyTorch eager probably does similar or more. Wait, I have an idea: instead of reading global twice, I can do a tiled approach where I read a chunk into shared memory, compute sum for that chunk, then later reuse it for normalization. But I need the mean before normalizing, so I need two passes. I could do: Pass 1: Read data into shared memory, compute local sums per thread, reduce to mean. Pass 2: Read data from shared memory (still there), normalize using mean/inv_std. But shared memory stored data is volatile unless I wait for all threads to finish pass 1. Actually, all threads are in the same block so __syncthreads after pass 1 ensures data is in shared memory. Here's the algorithm: 1. Each thread reads its assigned elements from global memory into shared memory `sdata`. 2. __syncthreads 3. Each thread reads from `sdata` and computes local sum and sum_sq. 4. Block reduction to compute group mean and inv_std. 5. __syncthreads 6. Each thread reads from `sdata` again, normalizes, and writes to global output. But wait, the elements assigned to each thread are strided: thread t gets elements t, t+blockDim.x, t+2*blockDim.x, etc. For 8192 elements and 256 threads, each thread handles 32 elements. We can store those 32 elements in registers! Then no shared memory needed for the data itself. Shared memory only needed for the reduction of sum/sum_sq. Let's do: 1. Each thread reads its 32 elements into an array of 32 floats in registers. 2. Compute local sum and sum_sq while reading. 3. Reduce across block using shared memory for just the sums (2*256 entries). 4. Broadcast mean and inv_std. 5. Normalize the 32 register values and write back. This minimizes memory bandwidth: 1 read + 1 write. Great! Let me write this kernel and test its correctness against PyTorch's GroupNorm. Actually, for correctness against PyTorch's GroupNorm, I need to know if PyTorch also computes sum and sum_sq. If so, my approach should match closely (within 1e-4). But if the conv outputs are the exact same, the norm should match to ~1e-5 unless PyTorch uses a different variance computation. Let me write and test it. Also, can I somehow get PyTorch conv output and immediately call my norm kernel without writing everything back in Python? Yes, in forward() I call `conv_out = F.conv1d(...)`, then `return self.cuda_ext.groupnorm_forward_cuda(conv_out, ...)`. Let me write this version.

callcompile_kernel { "kernel_code": "import torch\nimport torch.nn as nn\nfrom torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline\n\nCUDA_SOURCE = r'''\n#include <torch/extension.h>\n#include <cuda_runtime.h>\n#include <ATen/cuda/CUDAContext.h>\n#include <cmath>\n\n__global__ void groupnorm_only_kernel(\n const float* __restrict__ x,\n const float* __restrict__ gamma,\n const float* __restrict__ beta,\n float* __restrict__ y,\n int N, int C, int T,\n int num_groups, float eps, bool affine\n) {\n int n = blockIdx.x;\n int g = blockIdx.y;\n int tid = threadIdx.x;\n int blockSize = blockDim.x;\n\n int channels_per_group = C / num_groups;\n int c_start = g * channels_per_group;\n int total_elements = channels_per_group * T;\n\n int lane = tid % 32;\n int warp_id = tid / 32;\n int num_warps = blockSize / 32;\n\n // Each thread processes elements in strided order\n double local_sum = 0.0;\n double local_sq = 0.0;\n\n // First pass: accumulate sum and sum_sq\n for (int idx = tid; idx < total_elements; idx += blockSize) {\n int t = idx % T;\n int c_offset = idx / T;\n int c = c_start + c_offset;\n float val = x[((n * C + c) * T) + t];\n local_sum += (double)val;\n local_sq += (double)val * (double)val;\n }\n\n // Warp-level reduction\n for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) {\n local_sum += (double)__shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, (float)local_sum, offset);\n local_sq += (double)__shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, (float)local_sq, offset);\n }\n\n // Store warp sums to shared memory\n extern __shared__ double s_stats[];\n if (lane == 0) {\n s_stats[warp_id] = local_sum;\n s_stats[warp_id + num_warps] = local_sq;\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n // Block-level reduction of warp sums\n if (tid == 0) {\n double group_sum = 0.0;\n double group_sq = 0.0;\n for (int i = 0; i < num_warps; i++) {\n group_sum += s_stats[i];\n group_sq += s_stats[i + num_warps];\n }\n double count = (double)total_elements;\n double mean = group_sum / count;\n double var = group_sq / count - mean * mean;\n s_stats[2 * num_warps] = mean;\n s_stats[2 * num_warps + 1] = rsqrt(var + (double)eps);\n }\n __syncthreads();\n\n double mean = s_stats[2 * num_warps];\n double inv_std = s_stats[2 * num_warps + 1];\n\n // Second pass: normalize and write\n for (int idx = tid; idx < total_elements; idx += blockSize) {\n int t = idx % T;\n int c_offset = idx / T;\n int c = c_start + c_offset;\n float val = x[((n * C + c) * T) + t];\n val = (float)(((double)val - mean) * inv_std);\n if (affine) {\n val = val * gamma[c] + beta[c];\n }\n y[((n * C + c) * T) + t] = val;\n }\n}\n\ntorch::Tensor groupnorm_only_forward_cuda(\n torch::Tensor x,\n torch::Tensor gamma,\n torch::Tensor beta,\n int num_groups,\n float eps,\n bool affine\n) {\n int N = x.size(0);\n int C = x.size(1);\n int T = x.size(2);\n\n auto y = torch::empty_like(x);\n\n int blockSize = 256;\n int num_warps = blockSize / 32; // 8\n\n dim3 grid(N, num_groups);\n dim3 block(blockSize);\n\n size_t shared_mem = (num_warps * 2 + 2) * sizeof(double);\n\n const float* gamma_ptr = affine ? gamma.data_ptr<float>() : nullptr;\n const float* beta_ptr = affine ? beta.data_ptr<float>() : nullptr;\n\n groupnorm_only_kernel<<<grid, block, shared_mem, at::cuda::getCurrentCUDAStream()>>>(\n x.data_ptr<float>(),\n gamma_ptr,\n beta_ptr,\n y.data_ptr<float>(),\n N, C, T,\n num_groups, eps, affine\n );\n\n return y;\n}\n'''\n\nCPP_SOURCES = '''\ntorch::Tensor groupnorm_only_forward_cuda(\n torch::Tensor x,\n torch::Tensor gamma,\n torch::Tensor beta,\n int num_groups,\n float eps,\n bool affine\n);\n'''\n\n\nclass ModelNew(nn.Module):\n def __init__(\n self,\n in_channels: int,\n out_channels: int,\n num_groups: int,\n kernel_size: int = 3,\n stride: int = 1,\n padding: int = 1,\n dilation: int = 1,\n eps: float = 1e-5,\n affine: bool = True,\n ):\n super().__init__()\n self.in_channels = in_channels\n self.out_channels = out_channels\n self.num_groups = num_groups\n self.kernel_size = kernel_size\n self.stride = stride\n self.padding = padding\n self.dilation = dilation\n self.eps = eps\n self.affine = affine\n\n conv = nn.Conv1d(\n in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size,\n stride=stride, padding=padding, dilation=dilation, bias=False\n )\n norm = nn.GroupNorm(\n num_groups=num_groups, num_channels=out_channels, eps=eps, affine=affine\n )\n\n self.weight = nn.Parameter(conv.weight.data)\n\n if affine:\n self.gamma = nn.Parameter(norm.weight.data)\n self.beta = nn.Parameter(norm.bias.data)\n else:\n self.gamma = None\n self.beta = None\n\n self.cuda_ext = load_inline(\n name=\"groupnorm_only_v1\",\n cpp_sources=CPP_SOURCES,\n cuda_sources=CUDA_SOURCE,\n functions=[\"groupnorm_only_forward_cuda\"],\n extra_cuda_cflags=[\"-O3\"],\n verbose=False,\n )\n\n def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n out = torch.nn.functional.conv1d(\n x, self.weight, None, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, 1\n )\n\n if x.device.type != \"cuda\":\n if self.affine:\n out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm(\n out, self.num_groups, self.gamma, self.beta, self.eps\n )\n else:\n out = torch.nn.functional.group_norm(\n out, self.num_groups, None, None, self.eps\n )\n return out\n\n if self.affine:\n gamma = self.gamma\n beta = self.beta\n else:\n gamma = torch.empty(0, device=x.device, dtype=x.dtype)\n beta = torch.empty(0, device=x.device, dtype=x.dtype)\n\n return self.cuda_ext.groupnorm_only_forward_cuda(\n out, gamma, beta, self.num_groups, self.eps, self.affine\n )\n" }
